тАЬрдп рдПрдХ рдЗрддреН’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореИрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ– тАШ рдп рдПрдХ рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЖрднрд┐рдкреНрд▓рд╡рд┐рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердореЗрд╜рд╣рдирд┐ рджрд╢рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдердореЗрд╜рд╣рдирд┐ рдЪ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдВрджрд┐рдирд╕рд╡рдиреЗ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдВрд╕рд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗрд╜рд╣реАрдирд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рддрд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рддреЗрд╖реНрд╡рд┐рджрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ– рдп рдПрдХ рдЗрджреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд┐рдЧреНрдорд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрдГ’ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рен. рел) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЙрдкрд╣рд╡реНрдпрдирд╛рдореНрдиреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рд╣реЗрд╜рдкреАрджрдВ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдХреЗрд╡рд▓реНрдпрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ-тАЩ рдп рдПрдХ рдЗрджрд┐рддрд┐ рдордзреНрдпрдВрджрд┐рдирдГ ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. реп. рен) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

22 (463)
Indra
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Like the previous hymn, this one compares the current poet to previous genera tions of poets (see vss. 2, 4, 7) and asks Indra directly what in the sacrifice might please him (vs. 4 [cf. VI.21.4]). In fact, the same phrase is used in both hymns to introduce other questions: VI.21.6 t├бm pr╠еch├бntaс╕е тАЬ(the singers) asking about himтАЭ and VI.22.5 t├бm pr╠еch├бnt─л тАЬ(the song) asking about him.тАЭ In each case the subject (singers or song) seeks information about ways to make contact and find favor with Indra, though the anxiety seems less in this hymn than in VI.21.
The similarities between VI.21 and 22 extend to their final verses. The exhor tation to come here with his teams in VI.22.11 is structurally and semantically, though not lexically, parallel to two halves of the two final verses of VI.21, 11ab and 12cdтАФan interesting example of how a poet can expand an underlying formu laic sequence by inserting new material.
Otherwise, the hymn alternates verses praising IndraтАЩs qualities and deeds in list-like fashion (e.g., vss. 1cd, 2cd) and begging him for wealth and martial help (e.g., vss. 3, 8, 10). Stylistically it is noteworthy that in much of the hymn, particu larly at the beginning, the initial word of every half-verse refers to Indra (1a, c; 2a, c; 3a; 5a, c; 7a, c; 11a). In 3c, the first half-verse in the hymn not beginning with a word referring to Indra, the poet tricks us by playing on our expectations: the y├бс╕е тАЬwhoтАЭ could easily be Indra, as it was earlier (see 1a, c), but in fact has a different referent. The most complex verse syntactically is verse 5, which is perhaps fitting, as it describes the poetтАЩs own song.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЪрд░реНрд╖рдгреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рдкрддреНрд╕реБ рдПрдХ рдЗрддреН рдПрдХ рдПрд╡ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрдГ рдЖрднрд┐рдГ рдЧреАрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрднрд┐рдГ рддрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН рдЕрднреНрдпрд░реНрдЪреЗ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМрдорд┐ ред рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдкрддреНрдпрддреЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдирднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдкрддреНрдпрддреЗ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдореАрд╖реНрдЯреЗ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдГ ред рд╡реГрд╖рднрдГ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдгреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рддреНрдпрдГ рдЕрд╡рд┐рд╕рдВрд╡рд╛рджреА рд╕рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╛рджрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рджрд╛рддрд╛ рд╡рд╛ ред рд╕рджреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рдиреЛрддреЗрд╡реЗрдВрджрдВ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдкреБрд░реБрдорд╛рдпрдГ рдмрд╣реБрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЕрднрд┐рднрд╡рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рддрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдорднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМрдореАрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorify with these praises, Indra, who alone is to be invoked by man; who comes (to his worshippers) the showerer (of benefits), the vigorous, the observer of truth, the subduer of foes, the possessor of manifold knowledge, the mighty.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To him who alone is to be called by the separate peoples, to Indra chant with these hymns,
to the bull with bull-like strength who is master, the real тАЬreal thingтАЭ with many magic wiles, mighty.

Jamison Brereton Notes

To add to the similarities between VI.21 and VI.22 noted in the published introduction, h├бvya- is applied to Indra in the first p─Бda here, recalling 22.1b h├бvyam .. h├бvy─Б havante; note also purum─Бy├б- in b, a descriptor of Indra also in VI.21.2d (as well as nearby VI.18.12).

On s├бtvan- see comm. ad I.173.5.

Griffith

WITH these my hymns I glorify that Indra who is alone to be invoked by mortals,
The Lord, the Mighty One, of manly vigour, victorious, Hero, true, and full of wisdom.

Geldner

Der ganz allein von den St├дmmen anzurufen ist, den Indra besinge ich mit diesen Lobesworten, der der Herr ist, der Bulle mit Bullenkraft, der wahre Krieger, der verwandlungsreiche, ├╝berlegene.

Grassmann

Der einzig ist von Menschen anzurufen, den Indra preise ich mit diesen Liedern, Der als Gebieter herrscht mit Heldenkr├дften, der wahre, starke, zauberreiche Sieger.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo him the seven sages, our ancient progenitors, performing the nine days’ rite, were offerers of (sacrificial) food, celebrating with hymns the very strong (Indra), the humiliator of foes, the traverser of the heavens, he dweller in the clouds, whose commands are not to be disobeyed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To him (chanted) our earlier ancestors, the Navagvas, the seven inspired poets, inciting (him),804 VI.22
to him who catches up to the cheat, the surpassing one who stays on the mountains, whose speech is without deception, to the strongest one, with their thoughts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. lacks an overt finite verb. With Geldner I supply a form of тИЪarc, picking up the main clause verb of vs. 1, abhy ├аrca of 1b. The instr. mat├нbhiс╕е in our d is parallel to g─лrbh├нс╕е тАж ─Б╠Бbh├нс╕е of 1b.

The тАЬseven inspired poetsтАЭ (sapt├б v├нpr─Бsaс╕е) evokes the Saptarс╣гi, the тАЬseven seers.тАЭ I am not certain whether the phrase here refers to the Saptarс╣гi and, further, whether they are identical to the Navagvas; the numbers suggestnnot. It is worth noting IV.42.8 asm─Б╠Бkam ├бtra pit├бras t├б ─Бsan, sapt├б с╣Ы╠Бс╣гayaс╕е тАЬOur forefathers, the Seven Seers, were here,тАЭ with pit├бraс╕е, as here, as well as IX.92.2 с╣Ы╠Бс╣гayaс╕е sapt├б v├нpr─Бс╕е, where the Seven Seers are identified as v├нpra-s.

The interpr. of the cmpd nakс╣гad-d─Бbh├б- given in the publ tr., тАШwho catches up to the cheatтАЩ, cannot be correct. That tr. assumed a structure of the verbal governing cmpd type, like bhar├бd-v─Бja-, but the accent is wrong. I therefore now see that a conventional tatpuruс╣гa interpr., with the 2nd member an agent nominal governing the first, should be the correct interpr.; so Grassmann тАШden Nahenden vernichtendтАЩ, Geldner тАШder den Einholenden (?) t├дuschtтАЩ. (Curiously AiG does not seem to comment on this cmpd, despite its somewhat aberrant form) The cmpd thus conforms to the type hastagr─Бbh├б- тАШgrasping the handтАЩ, at least as to its 2nd member, but the first member appears to be the weak form of the pres. part. to the pres. n├бkс╣гati (тИЪnakс╣г тАШapproach, reachтАЩ). I do not know, offhand, of any cmpds formally so constructed, and I am further puzzled by the apparent sense тАШtricking / cheating / outwitting the one who approachesтАЩ. Forms of the root тИЪnakс╣г generally have benevolent sense, as in the medial n├бkс╣гate in this very hymn (5d), where the song тАШcatches upтАЩ to Indra, or act.

n├бkс╣гanti in this same Indra cycle, VI.34.3, where thoughts and voices approach Indra, strengthening him, so there is no apparent reason for Indra to тИЪdabh someone innocently coming up to him. I would emend the tr. to тАЬhim who outwits the one(s) approaching,тАЭ but still feel that the first member is concealing something I canтАЩt crack. Some light on the cmpd may be shed by the verb forms ─Бna┼Ы├║с╕е and n├бkс╣гate in the following vss. (4b and 5d respectively; see below), and this set of vss. seem to share preoccupations and themes. Michael Weiss suggests that nakс╣гat could represent the root тИЪna┼Ы тАШdisappear, destroyтАЩ, with -s- suffix and desid. meaning (тАЬwho deceives the one who seeks to destroy himтАЭ). This is semantically much more attractive than the suggestions given above, but I am dubious about the morphology. The root тИЪna┼Ы does not have a desid. at any period of the language, and in any case we should properly expect reduplicated *ninakс╣гa-. Moreover, non-caus. stems to this root have the intrans. sense тАШdisappear, perishтАЩ. The forms in the immediate vicinity cited above that belong to na┼Ы / nakс╣г тАШreach, attainтАЩ would also cause interference.

Note the presence of both тИЪdabh тАШtrick, cheatтАЩand тИЪdruh тАШdeceive, lieтАЩ, with Indra depicted as engaging in the former activity, but possessing speech that is ├бdrogha- тАШundeceptiveтАЩ. In 8a he attacks the тАЬdeceitful peopleтАЭ (j├бna- dr├║hvan-).

Griffith

Our sires of old,. Navagvas, sages seven, while urging him to show his might, extolled him,
Dwelling on heights, swift, smiting down opponents, guileless in word, and in his thoughts most mighty.

Geldner

Denselben besangen unsere Vorv├дter, die Navagva┬┤s, die sieben Dichter, ihn aneifernd, ihn, der den Einholenden t├дuscht, den ├Ьberwinder, der auf dem Berge haust, dessen Worte nicht tr├╝gen, den Gewaltigsten mit ihren Gebeten.

Grassmann

Ihn priesen einst die Neuner, unsre V├дter, die sieben S├дnger, st├дrkend ihn zu Thaten, Der Feinde tilgt, auf Bergen thronet siegreich, der Wahrheit spricht, den st├дrksten ihn, mit Liedern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe solicit that Indra for wealth, comprehending numerous descendants, followers and much cattle, and which is undisturbed, imperishable, and the source of felicity, such riches, lord of steeds, bestow upon us to make us happy.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This Indra do we beseech for his wealth, consisting of many heroes, of superior men, of much livestock,
which is not stunted, not aging, and is filled with sunlight. O master of the fallow bays, bring that here to elate (us).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lack of accent on the demon. in the phrase asya r─Бy├бс╕е is notable. Geldner tr.

тАЬum solche Reichtum,тАЭ clearly taking asya as modifying r─Бy├бс╕е, and Oldenberg (ZDMG 61.828 [=KlSch 259]) defends a similar interpr., saying тАЬder weitere Verlauf schildert dann den Reichtum ausf├╝hrlicher.тАЭ However, unaccented oblique stems of ay├бm are ordinarily pronominal, and that interpr. is readily available here: the asya can refer to Indra, who immediately precedes in a different case (├нndram).

On the y├бс╕е of p─Бda c as breaking the pattern established earlier in the hymn of reference to Indra, see the published introduction.

We seek that Indra to obtain his riches that bring much food, and men, and store of heroes.
Bring us, Lord of Bay Steeds, to make us joyful, celestial wealth, abundant, undecaying.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf, Indra, your worshippers have formerly obtained felicity, confer that also upon us; irresistible Indra, subduer of foes, invoked of many, abounding in wealth, what is the portion, what the offering (due) to you who are the slayer of the asuras?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Will you declare this to usтАФwhether ever before singers have obtained your favor, Indra?
What is your portion? What is the vital energy that belongs to a smasher of (rival) lords, you headstrong hammer-head, invoked by many, bringing many goods?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although there is no overt mark, I take initial t├бn no v├н vocaс╕е as a question (contra Geldner), matching the overt questions in cd and introducing the indirect question in the y├бdi clause; see also prch├бnt─л in the next vs. and the questions in the previous hymn, VI.21 3-4, 6).

The poet seems to be harking back to vs. 2 in 4ab and vs. 3 in 4cd. In vs. 2 the ancestral poets praised Indra, but the god is described as nakс╣гad-d─Бbh├б- тАШoutwitting the one(s) approachingтАЩ. Here the poet asks if previous singers obtained (─Бna┼Ы├║с╕е) IndraтАЩs favor. Although this pf. belongs to the root тИЪ(n)a┼Ы тАШattain, reachтАЩ, which is synchronically separate from тИЪnakс╣г тАШapproachтАЩ, the latter root is a fairly transparent enlargement or development of the former (see EWA s.v. NA┼Ъ1 , p. 28; Narten, SigAor. 160, Got┼Н, 1st Kl., 192), and, of course, some forms of тИЪ(n)a┼Ы have the root syllable nakс╣г (e.g., desid. ├нnakс╣гati, though see ├нyakс╣гati in the previous hymn, VI.21.3). I therefore suggest that ─Бna┼Ы├║с╕е implicitly responds to nakс╣гat- in 2c. With my new (and, I hope, more accurate) interpr. of nakс╣гad-d─Бbh├б- in 2c, I now think that vs. 2 implies that Indra may deviously rebuff the attentions of his praisers and have done so even to the legendary poets of the past. Here the poet directly asks the question if these previous poets (/singers) actually obtained (─Бna┼Ы├║с╕е) the favor they sought in approaching (nakс╣гat-) Indra, whose benevolence cannot be taken for granted.

In the 2nd hemistich the questions turn to IndraтАЩs portion (bh─Бg├б-) and his vital energy (v├бyaс╕е) in battle, but also refers to the wealth he may bring. The two cmpds p├║ruh┼лta pur┼лvaso respond to puruv─л╠Бrasya .. purukс╣г├│с╕е in 3d.

The voc. khidvaс╕е, presumably to a -vant-stem *kh├нdvant- (AiG II.2.896, or, less likely, *kh├нdvan- or *khidv─Бс╣Гs-), belongs to the synchronic root тИЪkhid, which, despite its relative rarity, displays a variety of senses centered around aggressive action. Since this stem is a hapax, itтАЩs difficult to know which of the senses is reflected here; Grassmann renders as тАШdr├дngend (so also EWA s.v. KHED), bedr├дngend, Geldner тАШAbzwackerтАЩ. The only RVic nominal form to this root is kh├йd─Б (3x), which in its clearest occurrence (VIII.76.3) means тАШhammerтАЩ or the like. I have evoked this sense here, in the English idiom тАШhammer-headтАЩ, thus forming an unjustified etym. figure in tr. тАЬheadstrong hammer-headтАЭ – тАШheadstrongтАЩ representing dudhra. Although the standard tr. are safer, the fact that the form is a hapax to a poorly attested root invites a more noticeable tr. than тАШpressingтАЩ.

I follow W. E. Hale (├Бsura-, 65) in taking asura- in asurah├бn- as referring to human тАШlordsтАЩ who lead forces inimical to us.

Griffith

Tell thou us this, if at thy hand aforetime the earlier singers have obtained good fortune,
What is thy share and portion, Strong Subduer, Asura-slayer, rich, invoked of many?

Grassmann

Das k├╝nde uns, wenn je zuvor die S├дnger, o Indra, deine Huld und Gunst erlangten, Was deine Gab’ und Kraft ist, wilder Dr├дnger, Asurent├╢dter, vielgerufner, reicher.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe whose ceremonial and eulogistic hymn is commemorating Indra, the holder of the thunderbolt, seated in his car, the accepter of many, the doer of many great deeds, the bestower of strength, proceeds promptly to acquire happiness, and encounters (with confidence) the malevolent.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The quivering, surging (song), asking about him whose hand holds the mace, who stands upon the chariotтАФabout Indra, whose song it isтАФ (him who is) powerfully grasping, powerfully ranging, taking on wild frenzyтАФ(the song) seeks her way; she catches up to the bulging one [=Indra].

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is beset with difficulties, starting with the syntax, on which see Oldenberg

The major problems are that there is no finite verb until iс╣гe in d and that it is unclear what the limits are of the rel. cl. marked by y├бsya in b. If we follow OldenbergтАЩs first option, that the rel. cl. occupies p─Бdas a-c, the rel. prn. (towards the end of b) is positioned far too deeply in the clause. His 3rd option envisions a discontinuous rel. cl. partly embedded in and partly following the main cl., with the rel cl. verb being n├бkс╣гate in d – a syntactic configuration that is simply impossible. His 2nd option, basically adopted by Geldner as well, takes the rel. cl. as limited to v├йp─л v├бkvar─л y├бsya n┼л╠Бg─л╠Бс╕е. This is more acceptable, though the rel. cl. would be definitely embedded, not only in the main clause but within a long acc. NP (t├бm тАж ├нndram [REL CL] tuvigr─Бbh├бm тАж). My own solution is similar to this, but limits the rel. cl. to y├бsya n┼л╠Бg─л╠Бс╕е; this not only better accounts for the position of the particle n┼л╠Бbut also diminishes the effect of the embedding, because brief nominal rel. clauses, roughly equivalent to izafe constructions, seem to be at least marginally acceptable in RVic syntax. See esp. y├│ v├нd─Бnaс╕е in the previous hymn, VI.21.2. ScarlattaтАЩs (208) tr. appears to follow the same analysis, with the rel. cl. limited to тАЬ[das Lied,] das nun ihm geh├╢rt тАжтАЭ The root noun cmpd rabhod─Б╠Б- is glossed by Scarlatta (208) in the first instance as тАШUngest├╝m, Gewalt, Kraft gebend, aufnehmendтАЩ, leaving it undetermined whether Indra bestows or assumes r├бbhas-, a question that Scarlatta discusses in some detail without coming to a definite conclusion. Since, as Scarlatta notes, there are several good exx. of r├бbhas- and related words as objects of medial ─Б╠БтИЪd─Б тАШtake, assumeтАЩ (e.g., I.145.3) and since the p─Бda in which the adj. is found seems to depict Indra on a rampage (tuvigr─Бbh├бс╣Г tuvik┼лrm├нm тАЬpowerfully grasping, powerfully rangingтАЭ), the medial тАШassumeтАЩ value makes the most sense. Although ideally we might want the preverb ─Б╠Бrepresented, root noun cmpds with the structure NOUN-PREV-тИЪ seem to be rare to non-existent. (Cmpds of the type tveс╣г├б-saс╣Г-dс╣Ы┼Ы- in 9b below arenтАЩt counterexamples, because, as the accent shows, the root noun cmpd saс╣Гdr╠е╠Б┼Ы- has been in turn incorporated into a bahuvr─лhi), and in any case the outcome of rabhas-─Бd─Б╠Б- would be hard to parse once sandhi rules had applied.

The verb of the main clause must be iс╣гe in d, but what it represents is uncertain. Grassmann (Nachtr., 1755) assigns it to тИЪiс╣г тАШsendтАЩ, identifying it as a 1st sg.; Oldenberg tr.

as 3rd sg. тАШer regt sich тАж anтАЩ, which I assume means that he assigns it to тИЪiс╣г тАШsendтАЩ, though he doesnтАЩt comment on either root affiliation or morphology. Geldner suggests a 3rd sg. either to тИЪi (built like stuс╣гe, acdg. to him, though stuс╣гe is overwhelmingly first sg.) or to тИЪiс╣г (which тИЪiс╣г he doesn’t say, though his tr. тАШsuchtтАЩ suggests тИЪiс╣г тАШseekтАЩ).

Lubotsky gives iс╣гe as an independent lemma (p. 321), with a question mark, no gloss, and 4 occurrences. As my tr. тАШseeksтАЩ indicates, I think it belongs to тИЪiс╣г тАШseekтАЩ and is a 3rd sg. A number of other forms to this root take g─Бt├║m тАШwayтАЩ as obj. (pres. ich├б- I.80.6, IV.18.10, VI.6.1; pf. ─лс╣г- I.112.16, III.1.2). But what is the form? Almost the only way to get a 3rd sg. in -e (outside of archaic forms like duh├й) is in the perfect, and as we just saw, other forms of the pf. of this root take the same object. I suggest that we do, or did, have a pf. here, whose expected form would be *─лс╣гe. This putative form with heavy root syllable would in fact work metrically here. See also IV.23.6 and X.20.7, where I suggest the same underlying form for the transmitted form with light root vowel; the suggested long vowel is a significant metrical improvement in both passages. (LubotskyтАЩs 4th ex. in VIII.46.17 is better taken as part of a cmpd. ├бramiс╣гe.) There are several ways to explain the short vowel. On the one hand, it can be wrongly extracted from combinations with preverbs like upeс╣г├й in I.129.8, whose correct analysis is upa ─лс╣г├й, but could also in principle contain *iс╣г├й. On the other hand, the dat. iс╣г├й to the root noun ├нс╣г- тАШrefreshmentтАЩ, found in nearby VI.13.2, 17.14, might have influenced it. Michael Weiss suggests that itтАЩs simply an archaic 3rd sg. middle pres., like duh├й just cited - which would cut the Gordian knot.

Stepping back from the formal difficulties of the vs., we can try to fit its contents into the context of the hymn. The vs. seems to express the same questioning anxiety as vs. 4: do the singers – and their song – succeed in reaching Indra and attaining his good opinion, or does he respond to their approach with disdainful tricks? While asking this question, the song seeks her way and approaches what sounds like an intimidatingly formidable Indra, hoping for acceptance and favor.

That we have moved from the plural male poets/singers of vss. 2 and 4 to the lone female song (fem. g─л╠Бс╕е) makes the mismatch of power all the clearer. The verb n├бkс╣гate in the final clause brings us back to nakс╣гad-d─Бbh├б- in vs. 2.

Griffith

He who for car-borne Indra, armed with thunder, hath a hymn, craving, deeply-piercing, fluent,
Who sends a song effectual, firmly-grasping, and strength-bestowing, he comes near the mighty.

Geldner

Nach ihm, dem Wagenfahrer mit der Keule in der Hand, nach Indra, dem die schwungvolle, befl├╝gelte Lobrede geh├╢rt, der den gro├Яen Griff hat, nach dem Vielausrichtenden, Mutleihenden fragend, sucht die Rede ihren Weg und gelangt zu den Starken.

Grassmann

Den Indra ruft das Lied, der steht im Wagen den Blitz im Arme, dem der rege Ruf gilt, Zu ihm, der stark ergreift und wirkt, der Kraft gibt, beeilt den Lauf es und erreicht den feisten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSelf-invigorated Indra, you have crushed by your knotted (thunderbolt), quick as thought, that Vс╣Ыtra, growing in strength by this cunning; very radiant and mighty (Indra), you have demolished by (your) irresistible (shaft) the unyielding, compact, and strong (cities of the asuras).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Growing in strength: ay─Б m─Бyay─Б v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бnam, by this guile or deception

Jamison Brereton

With this magic power (of yours), with the mountain [=mace] that has the speed of thought (you shattered) him who had grown strong through his magic power, you self-powerful one.
You boldly shattered even the immovable, firm fastnesses, o you of good might who confer abundance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

IndraтАЩs overwhelming power, viewed with some apprehension in the previous vss., is a positive force when it is exercised for our benefit against external foes, and the hymn now turns to this happier theme. The published translation assigns the instr. phrase ay─Б╠БтАж m─Бy├бy─Б тАЬwith this magic powerтАЭ to Indra, whereas Geldner and Oldenberg assume that the phrase goes with v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├бm and refers to Vс╣ЫtraтАЩs m─Бy─Б╠Б; Oldenberg is in fact quite scornful of the former interpr. However, see comm. ad nearby VI.18.9, where I argue that Indra is regularly credited with m─Бy─Б╠Бin this Indra cycle. See, e.g., 1d in this hymn and 2d in the previous one (VI.21.2), both with purum─Бy├б- qualifying Indra. It is also the case that this hymn contains hostile m─Бy─Б╠Б; see 9d. I therefore now think that m─Бyay─Б╠Бin this vs. has double application. Its tight embedding in the acc. phrase ty├бm m─Бy├бy─Б v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├бm does suggest that it belongs to Vс╣Ыtra, but the initial near-deictic ay─Б╠Б, outside that NP, refers, in my opinion, to тАЬthis (m─Бy─Б╠Б) right hereтАЭ – namely IndraтАЩs. I would therefore amend the tr. to тАЬWith this (magic power of yours) right here тАж (you shattered) him who had grown strong with his magic power.тАЭ The identification of the vajra with тАЬthe mountain that has the speed of thoughtтАЭ goes back to S─Бyaс╣Зa. Though the first hemistich lacks a verb, it is easy enough to supply тАШshatteredтАЩ from ruj├│ v├н in the 2nd half-vs. _________ 07
The predicated inf. paritaс╣Гsay├бdhyai has no clear subject, but vaс╕е must serve in this capacity, referring to the poets, who will perform this action with тАЬtheir newer insightтАЭ (dhiy─Б╠Бn├бvasy─Б). The model for this action is the previous poets referred to in 2ab who praised and stimulated Indra, here represented by the adverbial pratnav├бt тАШin the ancient way, as the ancients didтАЩ. The force of pari- in the infinitive must be to indicate that poets from all competing groups will try to pull Indra to their side.

Geldner renders anim─Бn├б- as тАШohne VorbildтАЩ (pattern, model), but there seems to be no support for this tr. The only occurrence of n├н тИЪm─Б that I know of in the RV is in the enigmatic creation hymn III.38.7d n├н тАж mamire, where it is paired with ─Б╠БтАж mamire (7a), with both verbs referring to the тАШmeasuring outтАЩ of creation and created things. There is another occurrence of the negated adj. anim─Бn├б- in I.27.11, but nothing in that passage pushes the word to mean anything beyond тАШwithout measureтАЩ.

Griffith

English translation:

тАЬ(I have undertaken) to spread around with a new hymn, as i was done of old, (the glory of) you, the ancient and most mighty (Indra); may that Indra, who is illimitable, and is a sure conveyance, bear us over all difficulties.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(It is) for you [=poets] to tug at him, the strongest one, from every direction with a newer insight, him the ancient one as the
ancients did.
Indra, who is without measure, the good conveyor, will convey us across all difficult depths.

Griffith

Him will we fit for you with new devotion, the strongest Ancient One, in ancient manner.
So may that Indra, boundless, faithful Leader, conduct us o’er all places hard to traverse.

Geldner

Ihn umfanget mit eurem neuesten Gebet, den Gewaltigsten, den Alten wie vor alters! Indra, der ohne Vorbild, der gute Fahrer, soll uns ├╝ber alle schlimmen Furten hin├╝berfahren.

Grassmann

Ihn setzt in schnellen Lauf den alten, starken nach alter Art mit eurer neusten Andacht; Er f├╝hre uns, der sichre F├╝hrer, Indra, der unermessne ├╝ber alle Drangsal.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMake hot the regions of earth, of heaven, of mid air, for the oppressive race (of the r─Бkс╣гasas); showerer (of benefits), consume them everywhere with your radiance, make the heaven and the firmament (too) hot for the impious.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Brahmadviс╣гe = br─Бhmaс╣Зa dveс╣гс╣нre, the hater of br─Бhmaс╣Зas; perhaps, a reference to the enemy or hater of the veda or of prayer

Jamison Brereton

You set ablaze the earthly and heavenly (realms) and the midspaces against the deceitful people.
Scorch them on every side with your flame, o bull. Enflame the earth and waters against the hater of the sacred formulation.

Griffith

Thou for the people who oppress hast kindled the earthly firmament and that of heaven.
With heat, O Bull, on every side consume them: heat earth and flood for him who hates devotion.

Geldner

Dem arglistigen Volke m├╢gest du alle irdischen und himmlischen R├дume, die Luftr├дume in Flammen setzen. Verbrenn sie, du Bulle, vollst├дndig mit Glut, versenge dem Feind des Segenswortes Erde und Wasser!

Grassmann

Dem t├╝ck’schen Manne z├╝nde an die Flammen, die auf der Erd’, im Himmel, in der Luft sind; Verbrenn ihn, Held, mit Glut von allen Seiten, dem Andachthasser mache Erd’ und Meer heiss.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBright-flaming Indra, you are the king of the people of heaven, and of the moving races of earth; grasp in your right hand the thunderbolt, wherewith, Indra, who are beyond all praise, you baffle all the devices (of the asuras).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You become the king of the heavenly folk and of the earthly, moving world, o you of glittering face.
Set your mace in your right hand, Indra. Unaging one, you fragment all magic wiles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme v├н dayate is often used positively, of distributing good things to deserving people; cf., e.g., III.2.11 v├бsu r├бtn─Б d├бyam─Бno v├н d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe тАЬdistributing goods and treasures to the pious man.тАЭ However, a few passages are, or can be, negative, esp. III.34.1 d├бyam─Бno v├н ┼Ы├бtr┼лn тАЬfragmenting his rivalsтАЭ (probably also IV.7.10). Here the dominant sense must be negative and the wiles must be Vс╣ЫtraтАЩs (and perhaps those of other enemies) тАФ though a positive spin is just possible as a second reading: тАЬdistributing your magic wiles,тАЭ that is, deploying his own m─Бy─Б-s widely. See comm. ad VI.18.9 on IndraтАЩs use of his m─Бy─Б╠Б-s in combat.

Griffith

Of all the Heavenly Folk, of earthly creatures thou art the King, O God of splendid aspect.
In thy right hand, O Indra, grasp die thunder: Eternal! thou destroyest all enchantments.

Geldner

Du wardst der K├╢nig des himmlischen Volks und der irdischen Welt, du von schreckhaftem Anblick. Nimm, Indra, die Keule in die rechte Hand, dann zerst├╢rst du alle Blendwerke, du Alterloser.

Grassmann

Du, Indra, bist des himmlischen Geschlechtes und, pr├дchtiger, der ird’schen Welt Beherrscher, So nimm in deine rechte Hand den Blitzstrahl; du, ewiger, vereitelst alle Listen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBrin to us, Indra, concentrated, vast and unassailable prosperity beyond the reach of enemies, and by which, wielder of the thunderbolt, you have rendered human enemies, whether D─Бsas or ─Аryas, easy to be overcome.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Set) here uninterrupted well-being for us, lofty and not negligible, for us to overcome our rivals, Indra,
(well-being) by which you will make the D─Бsa and ─Аrya obstacles easy to thrust away, o mace-bearer, and those from the Nahuс╣гas.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The main cl., occupying the first hemistich, has no verb; I supply dhiс╣гv├б from 9a, though any verb of providing, giving, bringing would work as well (see GeldnerтАЩs тАЬbringтАЭ). The contrastive pair d─Б╠Б┼Ыa- ─Б╠Бrya-, juxtaposed in c, is a species of merism that would seem to encompass all the types of human obstacles we might encounter; n─Б╠Бhuс╣г─Бс╣Зi in d appears to be an afterthought that focuses our enmity on a defined group within the larger whole.

Griffith

Give us confirmed prosperity, O Indra, vast and exhaustless for the foe’s subduing.
Strengthen therewith the Arya’s hate and Dasa’s, and let the arms of Nahusas be mighty.

Geldner

Indra, bring uns anhaltendes Gl├╝ck zur Feindebesiegung, gro├Яes, nicht gering zu achtendes, durch das du die dasischen, die arischen Feinde, die nahusischen spornstreichs in die Flucht schl├дgst, du Keulentr├дger.

Grassmann

Verschaff uns, Indra, zu der Feindbek├дmpfung viel grosses Heil, das dauernd sei, untilgbar, Durch das du Feinde, Arjer und Barbaren, die Nachbarv├╢lker fl├╝chtig machst, o Blitzer.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬInvoked of many, creator, object of sacrifices, come to us with your all-admired steeds, whom neither asura nor deity arrests; come with them quickly to our presence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Come here to us with the teams that bring all desirable things, you ritual adept summoned by many, you who receive the first of the sacrifice. (The teams) that neither a non-god nor a god will hinder, with them drive here swiftly in my direction.

Griffith

Come with thy team which brings all blessings hither, Disposer, much-invoked, exceeding holy.
Thou whom no fiend, no God can stay or hinder, come swittly with these Steeds in my direction.

Drum komm zu uns, o vielgerufner Ordner, mit reichbeladnen Wagenreihn, o rascher, Die nicht ein Gott und nicht ein Ungott aufh├дlt, mit denen komme schnellen Laufs zu mir her.

Elizarenkova
